## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics (classical mechanics: nonlinear oscillators)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is the acceleration and the available state variables are position x, velocity v, and time t, which matches second-order ordinary differential equations for (possibly driven/damped) nonlinear oscillators. Typical relationships express dv_dt as a sum of restoring forces (functions of x), damping forces (functions of v), and external forcing (functions of t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator (undamped, unforced): dv_dt = c0 * x (small oscillations around equilibrium with linear restoring force)
- Linear viscous damping oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (mass-spring-damper; viscous drag proportional to v)
- Driven linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (periodic forcing near/away from resonance)
- Nonlinear restoring force (cubic stiffness / Duffing core): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (hardening/softening spring behavior)
- Duffing with damping and drive: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t + c5) (bistability, jumps, chaos under strong drive)
- Pendulum equation (geometric nonlinearity): dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (large-angle oscillations; sinusoidal restoring torque)
- Quadratic (aerodynamic) damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * Abs(v) (drag dominated regime; dissipation ~ v^2)
- Coulomb (dry) friction damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * tanh(c2 * v) (approximate sign(v) friction with smoothing near v=0)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (self-excited oscillations with amplitude-limiting nonlinear damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - v**2) * v (velocity-dependent negative damping producing limit cycles)
- Parametric excitation (Mathieu-type stiffness modulation): dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (parametric resonance via time-varying stiffness)
- Nonlinear stiffness with saturating restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * tanh(c1 * x) + c2 * v (restoring force saturates for large |x|)
- Piecewise-linear stiffness (impact/stop or different regimes): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * Max(x - c3, 0) (hard stop/clearance nonlinearity)
- Energy-landscape form (gradient of potential): dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) + c3 * v (polynomial potential yielding multiple wells)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring-force symmetry: conservative oscillators often have dv_dt as an odd function of x (e.g., x, x**3, sin(c*x)); even powers of x often indicate asymmetry or bias forces.
- Conservative vs dissipative split: dv_dt ≈ f(x,t) + g(v,x,t) where g is damping; if g is proportional to v (or v*Abs(v)) it typically removes energy monotonically.
- Limit-cycle signature: terms like (c0 - x**2) * v or (c0 - v**2) * v indicate negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude (self-sustained oscillations).
- Drive identification: additive sin(c*t + phi) (or cos) in dv_dt indicates external forcing; products like cos(c*t)*x indicate parametric excitation.
- Geometric nonlinearity: sin(c*x) or combinations like x - (c*x**3) approximate large-angle pendulum behavior; expect near-linear for small |x|.
- Dry friction behavior: tanh(c*v) (or sign-like) produces near-constant-magnitude opposing acceleration for |v| away from 0 and a sharp transition near v=0 (stick-slip tendency).
- Multi-well/bistability: inclusion of x**3 and higher odd powers can produce multiple equilibria (effective potential with multiple minima), enabling jumps/hysteresis under drive.
- Impact/stop dynamics: Max(x-c,0) or other piecewise stiffness terms imply different acceleration regimes past a displacement threshold (non-smooth dynamics, higher harmonics).
- Quadratic drag regime: v*Abs(v) becomes dominant at high speeds; if dv_dt residuals grow with |v|, consider this structure over linear v damping.

Structure desc      : Additive combination of a time-harmonic term plus several v-weighted nonlinearities in x (v·x^2 and v·x^c7), a cubic in v, and a saturating tanh(v) term. Variables: t only appears inside cos; x only appears in the multiplicative factors with v; v appears linearly, cubically, and inside tanh. The two linear v terms are identical (c0=c4=-0.6320) so they combine to -1.2640·v; c1=0.3837 with c3≈-π/2 makes the harmonic essentially 0.3837·sin(t), while the dominant x-dependent shaping comes from +0.5254·v·x^2 and -1.041·v·x^1.351; c8=-0.0607 and c9=-0.0893 are comparatively small unless |v| is large (tanh saturates to ±0.0893). Approximate simplification (small |v|): y ≈ (-1.2640-0.0893)·v + 0.3837·sin(t) + 0.5254·v·x^2 - 1.041·v·x^1.351 (with a small -0.0607·v^3 correction).

GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - beta*sin(x)*v - c1*beta*v
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed) is:
\[
-0.0313132230839372\,v^3\;-\;0.657729448450456\,v\sin(x)\;-\;1.31545889690091\,v\;+\;0.383670562566156\,\sin(t).
\]
So any matching candidate must be able to represent **exactly** these four components and **no extra functional dependence**:
1) a \(v^3\) term with fixed coefficient  
2) a \(v\sin(x)\) term with fixed coefficient  
3) a linear \(v\) term with fixed coefficient  
4) a pure time sinusoid \(\sin(t)\) with fixed coefficient  
and it must not introduce \(x^2\), \(x^5\), \(1/x\), \(\cos(kx)\), \(\exp(x^2)\), \(\tanh(v)\), \(|v|\), etc., unless their coefficients can be set to 0.

Also, the time term in candidates is often \(c\cos(\omega t+\phi)\), which can match \(A\sin(t)\) by choosing \(\omega=1\) and \(\phi=-\pi/2\) (since \(\cos(t-\pi/2)=\sin t\)), and amplitude accordingly.

Crucial obstacle: GT has **\(v\sin(x)\)**. Many candidates have \(v\cos(kx)\) or \(v x^n\), etc. Only candidates that can produce \(v\sin(x)\) (directly, or via \(\cos(kx)\) with phase shift *in x*, which none provide because they have \(\cos(c\,x)\) without an additive phase) can match.

### Candidate-by-candidate analysis

1. \(c0 v + c1\cos(c2 t+c3)+ c4 v + c5 v x^2 + c6 v x^{c7}+ c8 v^3 + c9\tanh(v)\)  
Has \(v^3\), linear \(v\), and time cosine (can become \(\sin t\)). But **no \(v\sin(x)\)** term; also \(\tanh(v)\) must be zeroed (set \(c9=0\)), and \(vx^2, v x^{c7}\) must be zeroed. Even after zeroing, still missing \(v\sin(x)\). **No match.**

2. Similar: includes \(v^3\), linear \(v\), time cosine; extra \(v/x^{1/5}, v x^5, v e^{c9 x^2}\) can be zeroed. Still **no \(v\sin(x)\)**. **No match.**

3. Includes \(v\cos(c8 x)\) but not \(v\sin(x)\). Since there is **no x-phase parameter** inside the cosine (only frequency scaling), \(\cos(c8 x)\) cannot equal \(\sin(x)\) for all \(x\) by any constant choice (you’d need \(\cos(x-\pi/2)\), i.e., additive shift). So cannot reproduce \(v\sin(x)\). **No match.**

4. Same issue as (3): \(v\cos(c8 x)\) cannot become \(v\sin(x)\) globally. **No match.**

5. Only polynomial-in-\(x\) couplings \(v x^2, v x^{c9}\); no trig in \(x\). **No match.**

6. Same as (1) but without tanh; still no \(v\sin(x)\). **No match.**

9. Has \(v\cos(c8 x)\) (no phase) and \(v|v|\). Cannot get \(v\sin(x)\). **No match.**

10. Has \(v\cos(c8 x)\) and \(v|v|\). Cannot get \(v\sin(x)\). **No match.**

27. Has a mixed term \( \sin(c7 t+c8)\cos(c9 x)\) (not multiplied by \(v\)), and also \(v x^{c5}\). GT needs \(v\sin(x)\) and a *pure* \(\sin(t)\) term independent of \(x\). The \(\sin(\cdot)\cos(\cdot)\) term cannot be made independent of \(x\) unless its coefficient is 0 or \(\cos(c9 x)\) is constant (impossible for all \(x\) with real \(c9\)). So you’d set that term to 0, leaving no \(v\sin(x)\). **No match.**

28. Has \(v\sin(c8 x+c9)|v|\) which involves \(|v|\) and thus is not \(v\sin(x)\). Also \(\sin(c8 x+c9)\) could match \(\sin(x)\) by choosing \(c8=1, c9=0\), but the extra \(|v|\) makes it \(v|v|\sin(x)\), not \(v\sin(x)\). Must zero it, losing the needed term. **No match.**

29. Time terms: \(c0\sin(c1+c2 t)\) and also \(c6 v\cos(c7+c8 t)\) (a time-varying coefficient on \(v\)), which GT does not have. You could set \(c6=0\) to remove that. Remaining terms are linear in \(v\) and \(v x^2\), but still no \(v\sin(x)\) and no \(v^3\). **No match.**

30. Has \(v|v/x^5|\) which introduces absolute values and \(x\) in denominator; must be zeroed. Remaining has \(v^3\), linear \(v\), time cosine, and \(v x^{c7}\) but no \(v\sin(x)\). **No match.**

### Conclusion
Every candidate fails because none can produce the required **cross term** \(-0.657729448450456\,v\sin(x)\) exactly. Candidates with \(v\cos(kx)\) lack an additive x-phase parameter, so they cannot be globally identical to \(v\sin(x)\). Candidates with \(\sin(\cdot)\) in \(x\) (only #28) multiply it by \(|v|\), giving the wrong dependence on \(v\) over sign-changing velocities.

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the GT:

**GT:** `-0.0313*v³ - 0.6577*v*sin(x) - 1.3155*v + 0.3837*sin(t)`

The key structural components are:
1. `v³` term
2. `v*sin(x)` term
3. `v` term (linear)
4. `sin(t)` term

Let me analyze each candidate systematically.

**Critical observations about GT basis functions:**
- `sin(t)` can be written as `cos(t - π/2)`, so `cos(c*t + c)` with appropriate constants works
- `v*sin(x)` is a specific basis function - candidates need this or something equivalent
- The GT has NO terms like `v*x²`, `v/x`, `v*x⁵`, `v*Abs(v)`, `tanh(v)`, etc.

For a candidate to match, it must either:
- Contain `v*sin(x)` (or `v*cos(x+c)`) as a basis function, OR
- Have all non-matching basis functions set to zero while retaining the needed ones

Let me check each candidate for the presence of `v*sin(x)` and `v³`:

**Candidates with `v*cos(cx)` (which equals `v*sin(x)` when c=1 and phase-shifted):**
- Note: `v*cos(c*x)` with free constant c cannot equal `v*sin(x)` because `cos(cx) = sin(x)` requires `c=1` and a phase shift, but there's no phase constant in `cos(cx)`. Actually, `cos(x - π/2) = sin(x)`, so `v*cos(c8*x)` alone cannot produce `v*sin(x)` unless there's a phase shift.

Wait - `cos(cx)` with `c` free: if we set `c=1`, we get `v*cos(x)`, not `v*sin(x)`. We need `v*cos(x + phase)` to get `v*sin(x)`, but most candidates have `v*cos(c*x)` without a phase shift inside.

So `v*cos(c*x)` ≠ `v*sin(x)` for any constant `c`. This is because `cos(cx)` with varying `c` changes frequency, not phase.

This eliminates most candidates that rely on `v*cos(c*x)` to match `v*sin(x)`.

**Candidates with `v*sin(cx + c)` (with phase):**
- Candidate 28: has `v*sin(c8*x + c9)*Abs(v)` — this has `Abs(v)` multiplied, so it's `v*|v|*sin(...)`, not `v*sin(x)`.

**Candidates with `v*x^c` terms:**
- `v*x^c` with free `c` cannot equal `v*sin(x)` since power functions ≠ trigonometric functions.

**Candidates 45-50 with `v*x²`:**
These have `v*x²` but no `v*sin(x)`. Since `v*x²` ≠ `v*sin(x)`, these cannot match.

After careful analysis, **none of the candidates contain `v*sin(x)` or an equivalent form** (like `v*cos(x + phase)` with a free phase parameter). The candidates use:
- `v*cos(c*x)` (no phase → can't become sin(x))
- `v*x^c` (power function ≠ sin)
- `v*x²`, `v/x`, `v*x⁵` (polynomials ≠ sin)
- `v*exp(c*x²)` (exponential ≠ sin)

None of these can produce `v*sin(x)`.

Let me verify: is there any candidate with `v*sin(something involving x)`? Only Candidate 28 has `v*sin(c8*x + c9)*Abs(v)`, but the `Abs(v)` factor makes it `v*|v|*sin(...)` which is cubic-like in v, not linear.
